text:
I reviewed this recipe almost a year ago but I made some interesting changes and just had to share it with everyone on this site! I used the 1/2 cup brown sugar, 1/2 cup white sugar, 1/4 tsp. salt and plenty of cinnamon and nutmeg as before. However, I am always interested in making recipes healthier so instead of margarine, oil or butter I used 1/2 cup unsweetened applesauce. I often buy applesauce in those little single serving cups and one container is exactly 1/2 cup. Perfect for baking since you don't have to open a whole jar of applesauce. I added chopped walnuts as before but I was out of vanilla, so I tossed in about a Tbsp of dark rum. Wow!! That is the secret to butt-kicking banana bread!! Use good quality rum, such as Puerto Rican or Dominican rum. A good rule of thumb is..if you wouldn't drink it, don't cook with it! Same goes for wine. I cannot stop eating this bread and now I don't feel guilty because it's low in fat if you use the applesauce instead of oil or butter. I really hope someone reads this review and tries the rum version I have come up with. Enjoy!!

text:
This was exactly what I was looking for!  I had 3 overripe bananas that I was getting ready to throw out, instead the light bulb went off to look on Allrecipes for an easy banana bread recipe.  I chose this one based on the reviews and the simplicity of the ingredients.  The only slight changes I made was I used butter instead of margarine, switched the white sugar to half white and half brown, and cut back the flour to 1 1/2 cups instead of 2. I also threw in 1/2 tsp. of vanilla extract and a dash of cinnamon.  It turned out perfect in 45 min. (an hour would have dried the bread out) and it is dense and moist like banana bread should be!  Thanks Libby, I will probably make this weekly with my leftover bananas!

text:
I've never made a really good banana bread until I tried this recipe this morning.  I did modify some things--used real butter, half white and half brown sugar, added 1 tbs cinnamon, 1 tsp vanilla, and a dash of salt.  I didn't measure the bananas, but used the four I had on hand that were mostly black on the outside, soft and sweet on the inside.  Sprinkled the top with sliced almonds, since it's what I had on hand.  It baked up beautifully in exactly one hour.  What a great Sunday breakfast!

text:
The recipe is good, it's me baking the banana bread that is a work in progress!
I have asked members for tips that really helped: don't over mix, lower rack so that top of bread is halfway point in oven, my loaf dish is glass so lower temperature in my oven to 325 degrees and tent with foil if the top of loaf is getting too dark.  I did as others suggested modifying the recipe and used half cup white sugar/half cup brown sugar.

For years I have been putting over ripe bananas in the freezer. They do turn black and get very mushy when thawed, but they get mashed anyway. When you want to make this bread, just thaw a few on a plate and squeeze into the batter.  Whenever I see bananas on the "reduced produce" rack, I buy them and put them in the freezer for a rainy day.

This will definitely be my go-to banana bread recipe.

text:
This recipe was awesome, and so easy! My parents, siblings, and boyfriend have been devouring it. Soo good heated with butter, and the consistency of this bread is the best I've ever had. Moist, not too crumbly, rich.

My only changes were (I doubled the recipe): I didn't have margarine or very much butter, so I had to improvise and use a mixture of butter and applesauce for shortening. I also added 1 tsp of ground cinnamon and 1/4 tsp ground cloves.

Helpful notes: I found that 2 whole bananas=1 cup mashed banana.

I made 1 loaf and 12 muffins--the muffins were done in about 25 minutes.

A delicious basic recipe that should be in everyone's recipe box! The ingredient list is nice and short, and most of it is readily available in ones cupboard at anytime!

I made this bread but used 1/2 cup butter and 1/2 cup white sugar and 1/2 cup packed light brown sugar and I added 1 tsp. vanilla. I also used super ripe speckled banana's and coated the pan with a light layer of butter.

This was amazing! I was shocked to actually be able to find a recipe that didnt contain salt. I did change it up a bit. Some of the other reviews suggested vanilla and cinnamon. Sadly I discovered that I was out of vanilla so I used 1tsp of peppermint extract instead. I then added a dash of cinnamon as suggested. Then instead of using the cake pan I used three bread pans. In each of the three loaves I added different things. I added walnuts to one, dark chocolate and mint chips to another, and a mixture of all my leftover chips (white chocolate, butterscotch, and milk chocolate/peanut butter...whatever was in my cupboard) to the last one. Then I only needed to cook them for about 30 minutes. All in all...absolutely amazing! The walnut loaf is nearly gone and I dont expect to be bringing any home from Bible study tonight ;-)

text:
This is such an easy and versatile recipe - I've used it so often in the last few weeks, I know it by heart now. I make this recipe as mini-muffins (bake time is 13 minutes), and my 5 year-old absolutely LOVES them. They're sweet, but not too sweet - just perfect. And you can really play around with it, too - I've tried this recipe with applesauce, pumpkin and bananas, as suggested, but I've also used pureed canned peaches, pureed strawberries and also sweet potatoes. I bet just about any pureed fruit would work. My husband and kids had no idea they were actually eating healthy muffins! This one is a keeper!

I always seem to have overripe bananas on hand, but my banana bread was never turning out right. This was hands down the easiest and best recipe for banana bread I've ever tried. I followed a couple reviews by adding a bit of vanilla extract and doing half white sugar and half brown. I also used baking powder instead of baking soda. I used 3 overripe bananas. The bread came out beautifully and -- big plus, here -- it didn't collapse in the middle like so many of my quick breads and cakes do. I want to try this again with walnuts and/or chocolate chips. Delicious.

text:
This is a great starting point recipe and I did expand on it a little further. Instead of margarine I did use butter. I used 1/2 cup brown sugar and 1/4 cup white because I did want to try keeping the sugar down. I think even next time I might try just 1/2 cup of brown to see how it works. Instead of all purpose flour I used bread flour because that is what I had on hand. I also added a pinch of salt and tsp of cinnamon. I took it out and it was extremely crispy and was a little disappointed but it tasted good. I waited til the next day to try it again and the flavors had a chance to meld so it was really good! The crust part was soft and tasty and the inside was dense and moist. It did remind me of my granny's banana bread which I do like. I'm probably going to try some other recipes but this is such a good, easy, pure, basic recipe it's hard to beat.

I'm very happy with this recipe. I have made a gluten-free version twice now and it has turned out delicious! I just use gluten-free all purpose flour instead. I don't use margarine so I used real butter  and added 2 tsp of vanilla to the banana mix. I also followed other suggestions and used 1/2 c of brown sugar with 1/2 c of white sugar. I also just use whatever ripe bananas I have on hand, usually 2 or 3, instead of measuring it out. I've found that 45 min is ample baking time - 1 hr would be too long. This is a simple recipe that's a keeper!

text:
I was looking for a simple recipe, and only had two over ripe bananas. So, I made some revisions. Since I only had 1 cup of mashed bananas, I also added 1/2 cup of canned pumpkin in fear that it might turn out too dry otherwise. I also added 1 teaspoon of vanilla, a dash of cinnamon, and sprinkled some brown sugar on top before baking. The bread tested done at 55 minutes. It came out very moist, very pretty, and rose up nicely. My small family of three ate it up within a day. Love it with the changes that I made...

I really liked this recipe.  I did read others comments and followed some of their suggestions and added my own. As per another review Instead of 1 cup of sugar I used 1/2 cup of white and 1/2 cup of brown sugar.  I also added 1 tsp Vanilla and a pinch of cinnamon and 3 bananas.    I also used whole wheat flour instead of white and 1/4 cup of ground flax seed.  I only used 1 3/4 c of flour.  Next time I will try only 1 1/2 c of flour because of the flax seed.  It only took 50 min to bake at 325.  It tastes great, although not as moist as most banana breads.

text:
Very good banana bread! I made the changes that most readers suggested by doing half white sugar, half light brown sugar, reduced flour to 1.5 cups, used applesauce instead of butter, added 2 handfuls of chocolate chips, 1/2 tsp cinnamon, 1/2 tsp salt, 1 tsp vanilla, and 2 TBS spiced rum.  I baked it for exactly an hour and had no problems with it burning.  I checked it at 30 and 45 minutes just to be sure in case I needed to lower the temperature or cover it.  I used 4 bananas, 2 overripe and 2 ripe.  It had plenty of banana flavor, as the ripe ones stayed pretty chunky when I mashed them.  It is very moist!  I regret adding chocolate chips.  I think it makes it too sweet. The next time, I will omit the chips and add a little bit of orange zest.  Four stars because I really ended up not making the orignal recipe but a variation suggested by reviewers.

Moist and delicious! I will certainly make this bread again. Also, my picky son toddler son loved the flavor!  I made single serving muffins out of this recipe, and they cooked at 340 degrees for about 45 minutes. I sprinkled about 1/4 cup (total amount) chopped walnuts over the tops right before they were put in the oven. YUM! They toasted right up. text:
I think this bread is the best I have ever made!!  I did alter it like most of the reviews.  I split the sugars 1/2 cup white and 1/2 brown.  I added 1/2 tsp salt and 1 tsp of vanilla.  I noticed alot of reviews were complaining about bake time and doneness.  What I did was pour enough batter to make 6 muffins and  pour the rest in my loaf pan.  I baked the muffins at 350 for 18min. and the bread for 40min.  It was a perfect amount of time, moist but done.  I think if I would have poured all of the batter in the loaf pan It would have been hard to get the middle done with out burning  some of the top.  I highly recommend splitting up the batter.  My kids love to eat the muffins more anyways.  I have finally found the best banana bread recipe!

text:
I've tried other banana bread recipes that call for vegetable oil and using margarine or butter gives it a much better taste and not as greasy. I just made it again and modified the recipe like other reviewers. I doubled the recipe and used 1/2 c. margarine, 1/2 c. applesauce, 1 c. brown sugar, 2 c. AP flour and 2 c. whole wheat flour, added tsp vanilla and had a little over 3 cups of mashed bananas. Followed the rest of the ingredients and procedure. When mixing the dry ingredients into the egg and banana mixture fold with spatula until flour is incorporated.  Don't over mix. The banana bread will be moist instead of rubbery and dense.

I made a few changes to this recipes when I whipped it up --- Two tablespoons of applesauce in the place of two tablespoons of butter, one and a half cups of Raisin Bran as opposed to one and a half cups of All Bran, and a dallop of raspberry jam instead of the raisins, as I was all out --- But unforch, the finished muffins weren't nearly as sweet or as flavoured packed as I had expected, which was a little disappointing. I have been making this recipe for years. Although I have tried others I always go back to this  one. Instead of creaming the butter and the sugar I melt a stick of butter and add it to the wet ingredients. I use 1 1/2 c. of flour instead of 2 c. I don't measure the bananas. I use four bananas. text:
I think this recipe is amazing in its simplicity. I give it four stars only because I modified it so much to make it what we thought was fantastic. As another reviewer suggested, I used apple sauce instead of butter. I also added a dollop of reduced fat sour cream, but you could probably use plain yogurt as well. It REALLY added something special, a bit of tangyness, to the bread and I would highly recommend it! I used half whole wheat flour and half brown sugar. We also added a teaspoon of cinnamon,a generous bit of freshly ground nutmeg and 1/2 tsp. of vanilla. I wouldn't dream of making a bread like this without vanilla. We made two loaves, one of them with A LOT of chocolate chips, not measured but probably about a cup or more. So, soo good. We will definitely be making this again in the future.

text:
This was yummy and super easy!  Based on reviews I made several changes, but I think the most important thing I did was not to overmix!  My last banana bread was a disaster.  I read reviews warning not to overmix, so I mixed everything by hand. Here are my changes: 1) Instead of 1/2 c. margarine, I used 1/4 c. margarine and 1 snack pack Granny Smith Apple Sauce 2) For the sugar, I used 1/2 brown and 1/2 white 3) Cut flour to 1 1/2 c.  4) I added a shake of salt, cinammon and nutmeg and 1/2 tsp. of vanilla.  I couldn't find my bread pan so I made muffins.  Cooked for 35 minutes and they turned out perfect!  Delicious on a rainy day.  I saw a suggestion that instead of two cups flour someone used 1 c. flour and 1 c. oatmeal and I may try that next time.

I've been using my grandmother's banana bread recipe, but with instructions like a "pinch of this" and "a bit of that" my bread never turned out the same.  I tried this recipe and have been making it almost weekly for months now!  Every time it turns out perfect.  I do throw in a tsp of vanilla, 1/8 tsp of nutmeg and 1/4 tsp of cinnamon. I also reduced flour to 1 1/2 C and added 1/2 C old fashioned oats and then sprinkled a few on top before baking.  I made mini muffins.  They were so good and didn't last long.  I will make these again and again.  It's my new banana bread recipe.

text:
Hands down THE BEST banana bread I have ever made OR tasted!  I made a few alterations based on other reviews.  I used 1/2 white sugar, 1/2 dark brown sugar.  Real unsalted butter instead of margarine.  Added a tsp of vanilla extract and a tsp of cinnamon.  In a skillet I melted some butter and toasted some pecans with a little brown sugar.  I let those cool and then added them to the top of the loaf before cooking.  AMAZING!!!  The banana taste is the main focus in this recipe and the bread comes out VERY moist!!  I am purposely going to neglect my bananas now just so I have an excuse to make this bread every week!

My husband told me last week that he didn't like banana breads. He gobbled it up last night! I followed some of the recommendations of using 1/2 white, 1/2 brown sugar. I added 1 tsp of cinnamon, but I think the next time I make this, I will reduce that amount--it over powers the rest of the flavors for me. I only had 2 bananas, next time I'll add another, I like a strong banana flavor. I did add one more ingredient on my own, rather than vanilla, I added 1 tsp of almond extract to give it a little nutty flavor without having to add the nuts. It tastes great! I didn't give this bread the full five stars though because I wasn't too thrilled with the texture, a little dry, and the top got burnt after 50 minutes of cooking. I wanted to take it out earlier when the top started darkening, but the middle was still gooey. This was my first time making banana bread, so I still want to experiment with other recipies.

text:
I borrowed ideas from other reviewers and came up with these mods: I subbed coconut oil for margarine, I used 1/2 c. white sugar, 1/4 c. dark brown sugar, 1/4 c. coconut palm sugar. I also added 1 tsp cinnamon, 1/2 tsp salt and about 1/4 -1/2 tsp fresh grated nutmeg to dry ingredients.  After adding bananas to egg mixture, I threw in 1 tsp pure vanilla and 2 tsp dark rum. 
I stirred 1/2 c. chopped walnuts into the flour mixture before adding to banana mixture. That way they did  not sink to the bottom of the batter. I baked in a 9x5 loaf pan and it was done in about 40 minutes at 350. I have a Monogram dual fuel oven and it cooks rather fast. I will give it more stars after I taste it - tomorrow! It is always better after sitting overnight. Thanks everyone, for the inspiration to try this.

UPDATE 7/29/2016 - One week later we are still eating this bread. Wrapped in foil and kept in the refrigerator, it is better and moister than it was when first made. It is delicious lightly toasted with butter, or eaten cold by itself.  I changed the review to 5 stars even though I changed it. I want this bread all the time now!

text:
This is an EXCELLENT basic banana bread. You can add to it and make it even better. Here were my changes: I used butter instead of margarine, I used half white, half brown sugars, I only used 1.5c all purpose flour and added 1/2 c. rolled oats. I only had 2 ripe bananas so I also added nearly 1/2 c. sour cream. I also added a 1/2 tsp salt, cinnamon, and an additional 1 tsp of vanilla. Additionally, I added some nearly rotten chopped strawberries (probably a cup), and I made a white, brown sugar and cinnamon mix to line my pan with. I sprinkled the leftover on top of the bread. This gave it a great, slightly crusty edge. I know, it seems like a lot of changes, but I wanted to pizzazz it up. It was AMAZING!!!

text:
I love this basic recipe, so many variations on the reviews! I didn't have any all purpose flour on hand (I know crazy..) so I decided to experiment with some of my leftover flours from my little gluten free stint. I mixed 1 cup of sweet rice flour and 1 cup of whole wheat flour. I did 1/2 and 1/2 with brown sugar and white sugar. Added a little vanilla extract with 2 SUPER ripe bananas. DELICIOUS! I would actually recommend to anyone that has sweet rice flour on hand to try it this way once. It makes the banana bread extra moist but still firm enough to handle (it reminds me of a cinnamon bun but a banana gooey cinnamon bun!!). I know it sounds like a weird combo, but I am going to make all my banana bread this way now! Yay for discoveries! Thanks for the inspirational recipe!

Excellent banana bread! I made mini muffins which took about 12 minutes and regular muffins which took 25 minutes.  for a moister bread, I only used 1&1/2 cups of flour instead of 2. I also used 1/4 tsp salt and butter instead of margarine. Also, I recommend combining a 1/2 cup brown sugar and a 1/2 cup white sugar to cream with the butter instead of just white sugar. To finalize these, I mixed in chocolate chips and I sprinkled a little cinnamon on each muffin before baking. They are amazing! Next time, I will try adding peanut butter to these as well. Thanks for the recipe!

I used 4 medium sized bananas (roughly equivalent to 2 cups), and found that it wasn't as "banana"y as most banana breads I have had before, next time I think I'll try a recipe that calls for more banana.  I also made the mistake of following "MomSavedByGrace"s review on the recipe page and let it cook for 45 minutes so that it would not dry out too much per other people's reviews.  Although two toothpicks stuck in the center came out clean, after I let it cool I noticed that the entire middle of the bread had not cooked.  In the end I had to throw it out after only being able to salvage an end piece.  It did smell wonderful cooking though.

Fantastic. I've tried more banana bread recipes than I can recall. I'll probably stick with this one with the modifications I picked up from other reviewers. I substituted 1/2 cup of cinnamon applesauce for the butter, I added about 1/2 cup of chopped walnuts, and 1 tbsp of good dark rum. I also did 1/2 cup white sugar, 1/2 cup brown sugar. This turned out excellent. It took about 1 1/2 hours to bake up but banana bread always takes extra time in my oven. Anyway, this is a delicious recipe. Definitely a keeper.

text:
This recipe is "fool proof".  I was teaching my five year old granddaughter how to bake and the phone rang.  I came back and we put the bread in the oven.  Ten minutes later, I realized we had left out the margarine.  I quickly melted it and took the bread out of the oven, stirred  in the margarine, and continued to bake.  The bread was still delicious. (I don't reccomend this technique, however).  When the loaf came out of the oven the center was still a bit moist so I microwaved the entire loaf for about 60 seconds, something I have done successfully before with dense breads. I feel this is better than browning the edges to death. I did use half white and half brown sugar,and added vanilla, salt and 1 1/2 cups flour and 1/2 cup oatmeat. I also sprinkled the bread with chopped walnuts and oatmeal.  Thanks Lilbby, this is a great starting point recipe.

This was the recipe I used for my first time making Banana Bread, and it turned out great!! I ended up using 3 over-ripe bananas, a little more than the required 1 1/2 cups, and I decided to substitute butter for margarine. I also sprinkled a brown sugar/white sugar mix on the greased pan before pouring in the batter. This recipe was very quick, and will definately be used again! Thank you :-)

I made this banana bread with just a few changes. First, I detest margarine in anything because it's fake food so I used butter instead. Next, I had four brown bananas that were quickly going downhill, so I used all four. Then, as recommended by another reviewer I used two tablespoons of dark rum. I also reduced the white sugar to 1/2 a cup and add 1/2 cup of brown sugar. Next, 1/2 tsp of salt and 1 tsp of cinnamon. OMG! This was just out of this world! I made one for a friend of mine who brought it to her workplace. She called me while she was eating it and told me it was the best she had ever tasted...and her co-workers with whom she shared the bread were raving about it. Thank you!  The four bananas made the bread moister and the rum sent it over the moon. Wow!

None
text:
I've made this recipe many, many times. It's absolutely delicious as stated. However, don't even bother making it (or any other banana bread) if your bananas aren't super ripe. It makes the bread extremely bland. I know, because I rushed things at Christmas and ended up with a dozen bland little mini-loaves. (By the way, this recipe makes 4 mini loaves.) Also, the margarine is a good idea, as it keeps the bread more moist than butter would, so don't substitute. I've tried making this bread with 1/2 brown sugar, but found that the difference in flavor (as long as the bananas are ripe) did not warrant the additional measuring. This recipe is so good, and so easy, that I have memorized it from making it so many times. =) It makes me feel like a grandma with a special heirloom recipe that no one would believe is actually really easy!

text:
Not the best, but pretty good with a few changes that were suggested by other reviewers. I added 1 tsp vanilla, 1/2 tbs cinnamon, used 1/2 white sugar, 1/2 brown. I didn't measure my banana, but I used 4. It baked for about 55 minutes, and I had to cover it after about 35 mins because it was browning too quickly, probably my oven though. I think this would probably be very bland as written. Also, definitely better after being refrigerated overnight, it wasn't very good still warm from the oven for some reason. Quick and easy to mix up, and good enough to eat.

text:
This is a very nice basic banana bread.  I certainly wouldn't call it the "best," but it is the easiest.  Based on suggestions from other reviewers, I used half white and half brown sugar.  I also used about 2 cups of bananas instead of 1 1/2 and added 1/2 teaspoon of cinnamon.  Although it's not quite as flavorful as I like, it is very nice.  If you're looking for something really simple that tastes good, you probably can't do much better than this recipe.

This is really good... I'm happy I didn't write a review right away because for some reason, it didn't taste so good when it was warm, but after it had been in the fridge for a while it tasted much better! It's such an easy recipe- i prepared the batter at 11 o'clock at night when I saw how black my bananas were and didn't think they would last another day, even for baking :@)I put the batter in the fridge and baked it in the morning in two narrow loaf pans, and it took about 40 minutes to bake.I used canola oil instead of margarine, and used three bananas (because that's what I had).I will definately add another banana next time. This was a great starter recipe. I follwed some suggestions from other reviewers. I split the sugar so it was 1/2 white and 1/2 brown sugar. I halved the butter and used applesauce for the other half.  I also added some cinnamon and vanilla.  I made 4 mini loaves with this recipe and had enough dough left over to make another 2 mini loaves.  Keep an eye on it in the oven if you stray from the regular loaf pan size.  I would make again when I have bananas that are going bad.

country:
None
text:
I give this recipe 5 stars as a good, easy basic recipe with lots of room for change if desired. I opted to use half butter and half applesauce and added a half teaspoon of cinnamon, but think it could use more. I like that the recipe calls for the banana measured in cups, rather than just calling for 3 or 4 bananas. Fruit comes in so many different sizes, and I needed about 5 ripe bananas to get 1&1/2 cups. When baking breads, cookies, or cakes, experience has taught me to start checking doneness at least 15 minutes earlier than the recipe calls for, due to variations in ingredients and oven temperatures and kind of pans used. Glad I did the toothpick test 20 minutes earlier. I always use an oven thermometer and used the temp called for, but no way it would have taken an hour.  I covered it in foil to finish it off for a few additional minutes, and dropped the oven temp 25 degrees. It still turned out nice and moist, but only needs about 40 to 50 minutes at 350. I will use this recipe again, but will probably use all applesauce rather than butter or margarine, and add more cinnamon and maybe even add some raisins and pecans or walnuts.

text:
I loved this recipe, only I too added my own twist by making it gluten free and still the best darn banana bread anyone I know has wrapped their lips around! Thankyou for the beginning of my all new glutin free beads and various recipes, dedicated to glutin free eating without losing a spec of the moisture or taste. I hope someone tries this, because I really want others to see just how amazing it is.
Using this recipe :
Use 8 ripe bananas
Double everything else. 
A cup of chopped walnuts of you like them. 
Use 3t vanella
Use glutin free Paleo flour, which is a blend of Almond flower, arrowroot starch, coconut & tapioca flours. 
I don't know anything about how to give the exact amounts in the bread. That part you'll have to figure out for yourself. Also, I use parchment paper because it's all I've ever used. It certainly always does right by me. 
Enjoy, and somebody please give this a shot! 
Thanks, Ginger 
Feel free to subsatute butter with apple sauce. 
Cook 50mins and check. Actually if check at 40.you want it just to the point of your pick chiming out clean. Not 5 mins after.
Ps I've tried to add photos three times unsuccessfully. Bummer.

text:
O M G!!! I would give this 10 stars if I could!!! I used the recipe as a base with my own additions. I used 6 overly ripe bananas. I added 2 tsp of vanilla extract. We love to really taste our vanilla! I added 1/2 tsp of salt based on another viewers suggestion. I also added 1/2 tsp of cinnamon. I used 1/2 cup of white sugar and 1/2 cup of brown sugar and threw in some walnuts . I buttered my mini loaf pan and dusted it with a cinnamon and sugar mix. As an experiment, I mixed blueberries in one of the loaves.  I baked them for 45 minutes at 350. The smell permeated the house amazingly! I removed 4 beautiful loaves and placed them on the cooling rack to cool. Well, they only cooled for a few minutes before we tore into them. The bread was super moist and dense. The best part was that beautiful cinnamon and sugar crust around the bread. The blueberry loaf was the ultimate!!!!!! This is now a staple for our household!!! Did I forget to tell you that I put the cinnamon and sugar mix over the top too???!!!I tried another banana bread recipe from this site and I couldnt taste hardly any banana!!! This was soooooo delicious and even better the next day!!! Thank you all for your reviews and sharing your modifications!!! They always help me make recipes to my familys liking and we end up with new recipes that we all enjoy!!!!

text:
I make this in a 6-cup bundt pan in my Instant Pot pressure cooker. I add 1-cup of chopped walnuts as we like them and it just adds a nice touch. Following general directions for this appliance (2-cup water in bottom of pot, place bundt pan on trivet), cover bread lightly with parchment paper and foil, bake on high medium pressure for 45 minutes and 10-minute natural pressure release, then release remaining pressure. Cool in the pan completely then turn out. This makes the bread extremely moist, almost like a cake. Yummy. Hubby likes it topped with whipped cream. I would recommend this recipe as written, but add nuts if its your thing.

Delicious! I added walnuts, used four bananas and 1 tsp. of baking powder and baking soda. If your bread is bland and dry either you're mixing it too much, your oven runs hotter than the temp on the dial and/or you didn't use enough banana. You could probably safely use up to five medium bananas in this recipe before it gets too mushy. If it's too sweet, only use as half cup of brown sugar.

I made this for the first time and I followed many tips given. I didn't measure bananas I used five, I hade some extra ripe frozen ones in the fridge. I used half brown sugar and white sugar. I didn't have eggs so I used organic flaxseed as a substitute and I added almond extract since I was out of vanilla. I also used a cup of oats in place of a cup of flour. My own added 'tis bits is I made a brown sugar and cinnamon crumble for the top and added some of my powdered organic peanut butter. You can't taste the peanut butter flavor at all but I didn't add a lot. The cake is super moist and full of banana flavor this would be perfect to serve with coffee in the morning. You can add all your own sparkle on this recipe and it still will come out great, you can't mess this one up.

text:
The texture was great, it looked and smelled perfect, and the taste was also good. We liked it. I'll be experimenting with it and making it again many times to come.

Based off other reviews and personal taste, I did half and half brown sugar and white sugar, added 1 tbs cinnamon, 1/4 tsp salt, 1 tsp vanilla, and 1/2 tsp almond extract. I also got distracted while mashing bananas and didn't get a proper measurement, so I just used 5 large (ripe) bananas.

The main thing I intend to do the next time I bake this is to double the cinnamon, vanilla, and almond extracts. Maybe add a little bit of nutmeg for an extra kick. Just a personal preference.

text:
Very delicious, simple recipe! I like very soft and moist bread, so I made the following changes:

- Added 1 tsp. vanilla
- Added 1/4 c. sour cream
- Used closer to 2 1/4 c. of bananas

I made both a loaf and muffins with this, and they turned out wonderful! You can also add chocolate chips or nuts; I usually coat them in flour before I mix them in the dough, to keep them from falling to the bottom of the pan.

I normally make it exactly as directed, adding chocolate chips and walnuts... this time I attempted to make these vegan.  Lesson learned!!!  Eggs and real butter are just so much better, however it's definitely an acceptable vegan/egg-free/dairy free option using EnerG egg replacer.  I prefer this recipe over the other banana bread recipes because of the ingredient simplicity...less is more.  I always have these basic ingredients on hand.

text:
Moist and less dense than our usual recipe, very delicious.  Notes for me:  1/2 white & 1/2 brown sugars, 1/4 tsp salt, 1 tsp cinnamon, dash of nutmeg, 1 tsp vanilla seeds in syrup, 2 cups bananas, 1/4 cup chocolate chips, butter.  Ran out of flour, used 1/2 cup self-rising.  Sift all dry together, mix all wet together, make well & combine w hands, gently add chips.  Bake at 350/45min. Let cool 30min b/f serving.

text:
I've made this several times and it's a great recipe.  I even use it with plantain.  Using plantain or with bananas which are still a bit firm, I saute them in butter until soft enough to mash.  Plantain tends to be a little more fibrous than banana, so it makes a few fruit chunks in the loaf, which for me is all to the good.  I also add a teaspoon of vanilla, sometimes some cinnamon or nutmeg.  I like to add chopped nuts, but they are so expensive here on the island that I don't bother.

text:
I used 1 1/2 cups of flour and 1/2 cup of Malt-O-Meal which is the same as Cream of Wheat.  I also ran out of bananas.  I thought I had 3 but only had 2.  My mashed bananas equalled 1 cup so I mashed up 1/2 cup of canned peaches (2 snack cups).  I was also a tad short of margarine and made up the difference (about 1/8 cup) of apple sauce.  I threw in 1/2 teaspoon of baking spice and another 1/2 teaspoon of cinnamon plus 1 teaspoon of vanilla.  I baked the bread on the lowest rack for one hour. Well,  I thought this bread was going to be a disaster.  It turned out perfectly.  It is moist and dense.  The banana and peaches really compliment each other.  Great recipe.  I can't believe how so many substitutions can result in such a wonderful bread.

This was very good and will definitely be my go to banana bread recipe.  I tried to make it a little healthier since my son will usually eat it for breakfast. I cut the sugar down to 3/4 of a cup instead of the full cup. I also used 1/2 cup of white whole wheat flour and 1/2 cup of white flour.  This made the bread a little denser than we are used to, but it was still very good. I also added a dash of cinnamon and a tsp of vanilla extract. Thanks!

text:
I'm a bad baker...mostly because I improvise and don't like to follow strict directions, a bad combination when baking. I've made this recipe three times now, each with slight variations, and the third times a charm! Here is what I changed and how I'll make this for now on: I only had whole wheat flour in the house so I used 2 cups whole wheat...I was scared this would make the bread overly dense but it had the same consistency as the first 2 batches (when I used only AP flour). I used 1/2 cup of unsweetened applesauce and 1.5 tablespoons butter (for taste). Also, 1 cup sugar sounded like a lot so I only used 1/2 cup and it was plenty sweet. I only had one egg left in the house, so I used that and added @ a tablespoon of water to the mix because it was a tad dry. Using 1 egg instead of 2 didn't seem to make a difference in the final outcome (first 2 batches I used 2 eggs). I also used 1/4 tsp of salt in the third batch which really helped the pop the flavor (I didn't add salt in the first two batches). My 2.5 year old son and I Love this banana bread...we call it Banana Cake (since we don't really allow him much sugar, this is a big treat for him). Hubby won't eat anything with fruit, so more for us!!

text:
I love this bread. It is so tasty and easy to make. I had never made banana bread before this. It turned out great. I followed another reviewer and cut the flour to 1 1/2 cups, changed the sugar to 1/2 cup brown and 1/2 cup white, also threw in a 1/2 tsp of vanilla and a dash of cinnamon.  I couldn't taste any of those specific flavors in the bread but I think it helped round out the flavor. Also 45 minutes is all you need and around 35 my bread starts to get too brown on top so I pop it out and put tinfoil on it. Overall a great and tasty recipe. We make it almost every week with our left over bananas.

text:
I quickly skimmed through a few other reviews and made a few changes:
I made a double batch, used 1/2c butter and 1/2c applesauce, used 1c brown sugar and 1/2c white sugar, used 2c flour and 2c oats, used ~2c bananas and ~1c zucchini (I was short on bananas), also added a splash of vanilla, some salt, and some cinamon.  Also added a handful of sliced almonds and a handful of walnuts.
Baked in rectangular pan for 45mins.
Tasty and great texture!  Only complaint is that it is still a little too sweet for me -- will cut back on sugar even more next time.
